Both the album and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/It%27s_Only_Rock_%27n%27_Roll_(But_I_Like_It)" title="It's Only Rock 'n' Roll (But I Like It)">the single of the same name</a> were hits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Near the end of 1974, Taylor began to lose patience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The band's situation made normal functioning complicated, with band members living in different countries and legal barriers restricting where they could tour. In addition, drug use was affecting Richards' creativity and productivity, and Taylor felt some of his own creative contributions were going unrecognised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-micktaylorinterview_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-micktaylorinterview-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of 1974, with a recording session already booked in Munich to record another album, Taylor quit the Rolling Stones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Taylor said in 1980, "I was getting a bit fed up. I wanted to broaden my scope as a guitarist and do something else ... I wasn't really composing songs or writing at that time. I was just beginning to write, and that influenced my decision ... There are some people who can just ride along from crest to crest; they can ride along somebody else's success. And there are some people for whom that's not enough. It really wasn't enough for me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2177" data-file-width="1265" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg/170px-Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg/255px-Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg/340px-Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_and_Ron_Wood_-_Rolling_Stones_-_1975.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ronnie Wood (left) and Jagger (right) in Chicago, 1975</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Rolling Stones needed to find a replacement for Taylor and the recording sessions for the next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_and_Blue" title="Black and Blue">Black and Blue</a></i> (UK 2; US 1) (1976) in Munich provided an opportunity for some hopefuls to work while trying out for the band. Guitarists as stylistically disparate as <a href="/wiki/Peter_Frampton" title="Peter Frampton">Peter Frampton</a> (<a href="/wiki/Humble_Pie_(band)" title="Humble Pie (band)">Humble Pie</a>'s lead guitarist) and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> (ex-<a href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds" title="The Yardbirds">Yardbirds</a> virtuoso) were auditioned as well as <a href="/wiki/Shuggie_Otis" title="Shuggie Otis">Shuggie Otis</a>. Both Beck and Irish blues rock guitarist <a href="/wiki/Rory_Gallagher" title="Rory Gallagher">Rory Gallagher</a> later claimed that they had played without realising they were being auditioned, and both agreed that they would never have joined. American session players <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Perkins" title="Wayne Perkins">Wayne Perkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Mandel" title="Harvey Mandel">Harvey Mandel</a> also worked on much of the album but Richards and Jagger had a preference for the band to remain purely British. When <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Wood" title="Ronnie Wood">Ronnie Wood</a> auditioned, everyone agreed that he was the right choice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood2003174_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood2003174-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Wood had already recorded and played live with Richards, and had contributed to the recording and writing of the track "It's Only Rock 'n Roll". He had earlier declined Jagger's offer to join the Stones, because of his ties to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Faces" title="The Faces">The Faces</a>, saying "that's what's really important to me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaytress2003239_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaytress2003239-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a> went so far as to say he would take bets that Ronnie would not join the Stones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaytress2003239_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaytress2003239-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Wood committed to the Rolling Stones in 1975 for their upcoming Tour of the Americas. He officially joined the band the following year, as the Faces dissolved. Unlike the other band members, however, Wood was a salaried employee and remained so until Wyman's departure nearly two decades later, when Wood finally became a full member of the Rolling Stones' partnership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 1975 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_Tour_of_the_Americas_%2775" title="Rolling Stones Tour of the Americas '75">Tour of the Americas</a> kicked off in New York City with the band performing on a flatbed trailer being pulled down <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">Broadway</a>. The tour featured stage props including a giant <a href="/wiki/Phallus" title="Phallus">phallus</a> and a rope on which Jagger swung out over the audience. Jagger had booked live recording sessions at the <a href="/wiki/El_Mocambo" title="El Mocambo">El Mocambo</a> club in Toronto to balance a long-overdue live album, 1977's <i><a href="/wiki/Love_You_Live" title="Love You Live">Love You Live</a></i> (UK 3; US 5), the first Stones live album since 1970's <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Yer_Ya-Ya%27s_Out!_The_Rolling_Stones_in_Concert" title="Get Yer Ya-Ya's Out! The Rolling Stones in Concert">Get Yer Ya-Ya's Out! The Rolling Stones in Concert</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_23_July,_1975.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="800" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Rolling_Stones_23_July%2C_1975.jpg/220px-Rolling_Stones_23_July%2C_1975.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Rolling_Stones_23_July%2C_1975.jpg/330px-Rolling_Stones_23_July%2C_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Rolling_Stones_23_July%2C_1975.jpg/440px-Rolling_Stones_23_July%2C_1975.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_23_July,_1975.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tour of the Americas '75, 23 July 1975. Wood, Richards and Jagger.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Richards' addiction to heroin delayed his arrival in Toronto; the other members had already assembled, awaiting Richards, and sent him a telegram asking him where he was. On 24 February 1977, when Richards and his family flew in from London, they were temporarily detained by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_Customs" title="Canada Customs">Canada Customs</a> after Richards was found in possession of a burnt spoon and hash residue. Three days later, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mounted_Police" title="Royal Canadian Mounted Police">Royal Canadian Mounted Police</a>, armed with an arrest warrant for Pallenberg, discovered "22 grams of heroin"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rvr518_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-rvr518-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> in Richards' room. Richards was charged with importing narcotics into Canada, an offence that carried a minimum seven-year sentence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandford2003225_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandford2003225-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Later the Crown prosecutor conceded that Richards had procured the drugs after arrival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rvr_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-rvr-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the arrest, the band played two shows in Toronto, only to raise more controversy when <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Trudeau" title="Margaret Trudeau">Margaret Trudeau</a>, then-wife of Canadian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a>, was seen partying with the band after one show. The band's two shows were not advertised to the public. Instead, the <a href="/wiki/El_Mocambo" title="El Mocambo">El Mocambo</a> had been booked for the entire week by <a href="/wiki/April_Wine" title="April Wine">April Wine</a> for a recording session. <a href="/wiki/CHUM_(AM)" title="CHUM (AM)">1050 CHUM</a>, a local radio station, ran a contest for free tickets to see April Wine. Contest winners who selected tickets for Friday or Saturday night were surprised to find the Rolling Stones playing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandford2003227_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandford2003227-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 March, Richards' partner <a href="/wiki/Anita_Pallenberg" title="Anita Pallenberg">Anita Pallenberg</a> pled guilty to drug possession and incurred a fine in connection with the original airport incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandford2003227_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandford2003227-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The drug case against Richards dragged on for over a year. Ultimately, Richards received a <a href="/wiki/Suspended_sentence" title="Suspended sentence">suspended sentence</a> and was ordered to play two free concerts for the <a href="/wiki/CNIB" title="CNIB">CNIB</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oshawa" title="Oshawa">Oshawa</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rvr_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-rvr-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> both shows featured the Rolling Stones and <a href="/wiki/The_New_Barbarians_(band)" title="The New Barbarians (band)">the New Barbarians</a>, a group that Wood had put together to promote his latest solo album, and which Richards also joined. This episode strengthened Richards' resolve to stop using heroin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stonemag_68-6"><a href="#cite_note-stonemag-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It also contributed to the end of his relationship with Pallenberg, which had become strained since the death of their third child (an infant son named Tara). In addition, Pallenberg was unable to curb her heroin addiction while Keith struggled to get clean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandford2003232.E2.80.93233.3B_248.E2.80.93250_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandford2003232.E2.80.93233.3B_248.E2.80.93250-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> While Richards was settling his legal and personal problems, Jagger continued his jet-set lifestyle. He was a regular at New York's <a href="/wiki/Studio_54" title="Studio 54">Studio 54</a> disco club, often in the company of model <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hall" title="Jerry Hall">Jerry Hall</a>. His marriage to <a href="/wiki/Bianca_Jagger" title="Bianca Jagger">Bianca Jagger</a> ended in 1977, although they had long been estranged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although the Rolling Stones remained popular through the first half of the 1970s, music critics had grown increasingly dismissive of the band's output, and record sales failed to meet expectations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rockhall_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-rockhall-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> By the late 1970s, after <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> became influential, many criticised the Rolling Stones as decadent, ageing millionaires<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stonemag_68-7"><a href="#cite_note-stonemag-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> and their music as stagnant or irrelevant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMGsomegirls_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-AMGsomegirls-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1978.E2.80.9382:_Commercial_peak">1978–82: Commercial peak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1978–82: Commercial peak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This changed in 1978, after the band released <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Girls" title="Some Girls">Some Girls</a></i> (UK No. 2; US No. 1), which included the hit single "<a href="/wiki/Miss_You_(The_Rolling_Stones_song)" title="Miss You (The Rolling Stones song)">Miss You</a>", the country ballad "<a href="/wiki/Far_Away_Eyes" title="Far Away Eyes">Far Away Eyes</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Beast_of_Burden_(song)" title="Beast of Burden (song)">Beast of Burden</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Shattered_(song)" title="Shattered (song)">Shattered</a>". In part as a response to punk, many songs were fast, basic, guitar-driven rock and roll,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMGsomegirls_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-AMGsomegirls-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> and the album's success re-established the Rolling Stones' immense popularity among young people. Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_US_Tour_1978" title="Rolling Stones US Tour 1978">US Tour 1978</a>, the band guested on the first show of the fourth season of the TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>. The group did not tour Europe the following year, breaking the routine of touring Europe every three years that the band had followed since 1967.</p>
<p>Following the success of <i>Some Girls</i>, the band released their next album <i><a href="/wiki/Emotional_Rescue" title="Emotional Rescue">Emotional Rescue</a></i> (UK 1; US 1) in mid-1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson201092_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson201092-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The recording of the album was reportedly plagued by turmoil, with Jagger and Richards' relationship reaching a new low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson201092_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson201092-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Richards, though still using heroin according to former keyboardist of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Small_Faces" title="The Small Faces">The Small Faces</a> <a href="/wiki/Ian_McLagan" title="Ian McLagan">Ian McLagan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLagan2000_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLagan2000-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> wanted to tour in summer or autumn of 1980 to promote the new album, which Jagger declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson201092_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson201092-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Emotional Rescue</i> hit the top of the charts on both sides of the Atlantic and the title track reached No.3 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson201092_128-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson201092-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_(1981).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="412" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_%281981%29.jpg/170px-Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_%281981%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_%281981%29.jpg/255px-Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_%281981%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_%281981%29.jpg/340px-Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_%281981%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_-_Keith-Mick-Ron_(1981).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Rolling Stones performing in December 1981</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In early 1981, the group reconvened and decided to tour the US that year, leaving little time to write and record a new album, as well as rehearse for the tour. That year's resulting album, <i><a href="/wiki/Tattoo_You" title="Tattoo You">Tattoo You</a></i> (UK 2; US 1), featured a number of outtakes, including lead single "<a href="/wiki/Start_Me_Up" title="Start Me Up">Start Me Up</a>", which reached No.2 in the US and ranked No.22 on Billboard's Hot 100 year-end chart. Two songs ("<a href="/wiki/Waiting_on_a_Friend" title="Waiting on a Friend">Waiting on a Friend</a>" (US No. 13) and "Tops") featured Mick Taylor's guitar playing, while jazz saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Rollins" title="Sonny Rollins">Sonny Rollins</a> played on "<a href="/wiki/Slave_(song)" title="Slave (song)">Slave</a>" and dubbed a part on "Waiting on a Friend".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Rolling Stones scored one more top 20 hit on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 in 1982, the No.20 hit "<a href="/wiki/Hang_Fire" title="Hang Fire">Hang Fire</a>". The Stones' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_American_Tour_1981" title="Rolling Stones American Tour 1981">American Tour 1981</a> was their biggest, longest and most colourful production to date, with the band playing from 25 September through 19 December. It was the highest grossing tour of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Some shows were recorded, resulting in the 1982 live album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Still_Life_(American_Concert_1981)" title="Still Life (American Concert 1981)">Still Life (American Concert 1981)</a></i> (UK 4; US 5), and the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Hal_Ashby" title="Hal Ashby">Hal Ashby</a> concert film <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Spend_the_Night_Together_(film)" title="Let's Spend the Night Together (film)">Let's Spend the Night Together</a></i>, which was filmed at <a href="/wiki/Sun_Devil_Stadium" title="Sun Devil Stadium">Sun Devil Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">Tempe, Arizona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Izod_Center" title="Izod Center">Brendan Byrne Arena</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Meadowlands_Sports_Complex" title="Meadowlands Sports Complex">Meadowlands</a>, New Jersey. Also in 1981, they played a concert at Chicago's Checkerboard Lounge with Muddy Waters, in what would be one of his last public appearances before his death in 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-1982, to commemorate their 20th anniversary, the Rolling Stones took their American stage show to Europe. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_European_Tour_1982" title="Rolling Stones European Tour 1982">European Tour 1982</a> was their first European tour in six years. The tour was similar to their 1981 American tour. For the tour, the band were joined by former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allman_Brothers_Band" title="Allman Brothers Band">Allman Brothers Band</a> pianist, <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Leavell" title="Chuck Leavell">Chuck Leavell</a>, who continues to perform and record with the Rolling Stones to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Music_Legends_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Music_Legends-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the year, the band had signed a new four-album recording deal with a new label, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">CBS Records</a>, for a reported $50 million, then the biggest record deal in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1983.E2.80.9388:_Band_turmoil.2C_solo_efforts.2C_and_decline">1983–88: Band turmoil, solo efforts, and decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1983–88: Band turmoil, solo efforts, and decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before leaving Atlantic, the Rolling Stones released <i><a href="/wiki/Undercover_(The_Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Undercover (The Rolling Stones album)">Undercover</a></i> (UK 3; US 4) in late 1983. Despite good reviews and the Top Ten peak position of the title track, the record sold below expectations and there was no tour to support it. Subsequently the Stones' new marketer/distributor <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">CBS Records</a> took over distributing the Stones' Atlantic catalogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_(1981).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="525" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_%281981%29.jpg/220px-Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_%281981%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_%281981%29.jpg/330px-Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_%281981%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_%281981%29.jpg/440px-Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_%281981%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_-_Charlie_Watts_(1981).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charlie Watts from The Rolling Stones; 11 December 1981, Rupp Arena, Lexington Kentucky</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By this time, the Jagger/Richards split was growing. Much to the consternation of Richards, Jagger had signed a solo deal with CBS Records, and he spent much of 1984 writing songs for this first solo effort. He has also stated that he was feeling stultified within the framework of the Rolling Stones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1985, Jagger was spending more time on solo recordings, and much of the material on 1986's <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Work_(The_Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Dirty Work (The Rolling Stones album)">Dirty Work</a></i> (UK No. 4; US No. 4) was generated by Keith Richards, with more contributions by Ronnie Wood than on previous Rolling Stones albums. The album was recorded in Paris, and Jagger was often absent from the studio, leaving Richards to keep the recording sessions moving forward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichards2010461_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichards2010461-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 1985, Jagger teamed up with rock musician <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> in the music video "<a href="/wiki/Dancing_in_the_Street#Bowie.2FJagger_version" title="Dancing in the Street">Dancing in the Street</a>", which was recorded as part of the <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> charity movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> This was one of Jagger's first solo performances, and the song reached No 1 in the UK, and No 7 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1985, the band's co-founder, pianist, road manager and long-time friend Ian Stewart died of a heart attack. The Rolling Stones played a private tribute concert for him at London's <a href="/wiki/100_Club" title="100 Club">100 Club</a> in February 1986, two days before they were presented with a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nzentgraf_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-nzentgraf-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Dirty Work</i> was released in March 1986 to mixed reviews despite the presence of the US Top Five hit "<a href="/wiki/Harlem_Shuffle" title="Harlem Shuffle">Harlem Shuffle</a>". With relations between Richards and Jagger at an all time low, Jagger refused to tour to promote the album, and instead undertook his own solo tour which included Rolling Stones songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneJagger_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneJagger-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandford1999268_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandford1999268-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Richards has referred to this period in his relations with Jagger as "World War III".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood2003247_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood2003247-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result of animosity within the band during this period, they almost broke up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneJagger_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneJagger-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger's solo records, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/She%27s_The_Boss" title="She's The Boss">She's The Boss</a></i> (UK 6; US 13) (1985) and <i><a href="/wiki/Primitive_Cool" title="Primitive Cool">Primitive Cool</a></i> (UK 26; US 41) (1987), met with moderate success, and in 1988, with the Rolling Stones inactive, Richards released his first solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Talk_Is_Cheap" title="Talk Is Cheap">Talk Is Cheap</a></i> (UK 37; US 24). It was well received by fans and critics, going gold in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989.E2.80.9399:_Comeback.2C_return_to_popularity.2C_and_record-breaking_tours">1989–99: Comeback, return to popularity, and record-breaking tours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1989–99: Comeback, return to popularity, and record-breaking tours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early 1989, the Rolling Stones, including Mick Taylor, Ronnie Wood and Ian Stewart (posthumously), were inducted into the American <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rockhall_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-rockhall-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger and Richards set aside animosities and went to work on a new Rolling Stones album that would be called <i><a href="/wiki/Steel_Wheels" title="Steel Wheels">Steel Wheels</a></i> (UK 2; US 3). Heralded as a return to form, it included the singles "<a href="/wiki/Mixed_Emotions_(The_Rolling_Stones_song)" title="Mixed Emotions (The Rolling Stones song)">Mixed Emotions</a>" (US No. 5), "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_and_a_Hard_Place_(song)" title="Rock and a Hard Place (song)">Rock and a Hard Place</a>" (US No. 23) and "<a href="/wiki/Almost_Hear_You_Sigh" title="Almost Hear You Sigh">Almost Hear You Sigh</a>". The album also included "Continental Drift", which the Rolling Stones recorded in Tangier, Morocco in 1989 with <a href="/wiki/The_Master_Musicians_of_Jajouka_led_by_Bachir_Attar" title="The Master Musicians of Jajouka led by Bachir Attar">The Master Musicians of Jajouka led by Bachir Attar</a>, coordinated by Tony King and Cherie Nutting. A BBC documentary film, <i>The Rolling Stones in Morocco</i>, was produced by <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Finch" title="Nigel Finch">Nigel Finch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Steel_Wheels/Urban_Jungle_Tour" title="Steel Wheels/Urban Jungle Tour">Steel Wheels/Urban Jungle Tours</a>, encompassing North America, Japan, and Europe, saw the Rolling Stones touring for the first time in seven years (since Europe 1982), and it was their biggest stage production to date. Opening acts included <a href="/wiki/Living_Colour" title="Living Colour">Living Colour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>; the onstage personnel included a <a href="/wiki/Horn_section" title="Horn section">horn section</a> and backup singers <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Fischer" title="Lisa Fischer">Lisa Fischer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Fowler" title="Bernard Fowler">Bernard Fowler</a>, both of whom continue to tour regularly with the Rolling Stones. Recordings from the Steel Wheels/Urban Jungle tours produced the 1991 concert album <i><a href="/wiki/Flashpoint_(album)" title="Flashpoint (album)">Flashpoint</a></i> (UK 6; US 16), which also included two studio tracks recorded in 1991: the single "<a href="/wiki/Highwire_(song)" title="Highwire (song)">Highwire</a>" and "Sex Drive". The tour produced the IMAX concert film <i><a href="/wiki/Stones_at_the_Max" title="Stones at the Max">Live at the Max</a></i> released in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>These were the last Rolling Stones tours for Bill Wyman, who left the band after years of deliberation, although his retirement was not made official until January 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tioos-chronicle93_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-tioos-chronicle93-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> He then published <i>Stone Alone</i>, an autobiography based on scrapbooks and diaries he had been keeping since the band's early days. A few years later he formed <a href="/wiki/Bill_Wyman%27s_Rhythm_Kings" title="Bill Wyman's Rhythm Kings">Bill Wyman's Rhythm Kings</a> and began recording and touring again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the successes of the Steel Wheels/Urban Jungle tours, the band took a break. Charlie Watts released two jazz albums; Ronnie Wood recorded his fifth solo album, the first in 11 years, called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slide_On_This" title="Slide On This">Slide On This</a></i>; Bill Wyman released his fourth solo album; Keith Richards released his second solo album in late 1992, <i><a href="/wiki/Main_Offender" title="Main Offender">Main Offender</a></i>, and did a small tour including big concerts in Spain and Argentina. Mick Jagger got good reviews and sales with his third solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Wandering_Spirit_(album)" title="Wandering Spirit (album)">Wandering Spirit</a></i> (UK 12; US 11). The album sold more than two million copies worldwide, going gold in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="964" data-file-width="1475" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg/220px-Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg/330px-Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg/440px-Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Platino_vodoo_lounge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Multiple platinum award for their 1994 album <i><a href="/wiki/Voodoo_Lounge" title="Voodoo Lounge">Voodoo Lounge</a></i>, on display at the Museo del Rock in Madrid.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Wyman's departure, the Rolling Stones' new distributor/record label, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Records" title="Virgin Records">Virgin Records</a>, remastered and repackaged the band's back catalogue from <i>Sticky Fingers</i> to <i>Steel Wheels</i>, except for the three live albums, and issued another hits compilation in 1993 entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Jump_Back:_The_Best_of_The_Rolling_Stones" title="Jump Back: The Best of The Rolling Stones">Jump Back</a></i>. By 1993 the Rolling Stones set upon their next studio album. <a href="/wiki/Darryl_Jones" title="Darryl Jones">Darryl Jones</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Sideman" title="Sideman">sideman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Miles_Davis" title="Miles Davis">Miles Davis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>, was chosen by Charlie Watts as Wyman's replacement for 1994's <i><a href="/wiki/Voodoo_Lounge" title="Voodoo Lounge">Voodoo Lounge</a></i> (UK 1; US 2). The album met strong reviews and sales, going double platinum in the US. Reviewers took note of the album's "traditionalist" sounds, which were credited to the Rolling Stones' new producer <a href="/wiki/Don_Was" title="Don Was">Don Was</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Voodoo Lounge</i> would win the Stones the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Album">Grammy Award for Best Rock Album</a> at the 1995 Grammy Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>1994 also brought the accompanying <a href="/wiki/Voodoo_Lounge_Tour" title="Voodoo Lounge Tour">Voodoo Lounge Tour</a>, which lasted into 1995. The tour grossed $320 million, becoming the world's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_highest_grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest grossing concert tours">highest grossing tour</a> at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> Numbers from various concerts and rehearsals (mostly <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_guitar" title="Acoustic guitar">acoustic</a>) made up <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stripped_(Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Stripped (Rolling Stones album)">Stripped</a></i> (UK 9; US 9), which featured a cover of Bob Dylan's "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Rolling_Stone" title="Like a Rolling Stone">Like a Rolling Stone</a>", as well as infrequently played songs like "<a href="/wiki/Shine_a_Light_(The_Rolling_Stones_song)" title="Shine a Light (The Rolling Stones song)">Shine a Light</a>", "Sweet Virginia" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Spider_and_the_Fly_(song)" title="The Spider and the Fly (song)">The Spider and the Fly</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LARS_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-LARS-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> On 8 September 1994, the Rolling Stones performed their new song "<a href="/wiki/Love_Is_Strong" title="Love Is Strong">Love Is Strong</a>" as well as "Start Me Up" at the <a href="/wiki/1994_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1994 MTV Video Music Awards">1994 MTV Video Music Awards</a> at <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a> in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVAwards_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVAwards-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> The band received the Lifetime Achievement Award at the ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVAwards_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTVAwards-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Rolling Stones were the first major recording artists to broadcast a concert over the Internet; a 20-minute video was broadcast on 18 November 1994 using the <a href="/wiki/Mbone" title="Mbone">Mbone</a> at 10 frames per second. The broadcast, engineered by <a href="/wiki/Thinking_Pictures" title="Thinking Pictures">Thinking Pictures</a> and financed by <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>, was one of the first demonstrations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streaming_video" title="Streaming video">streaming video</a>; while it was not a true <a href="/wiki/Webcast" title="Webcast">webcast</a>, it introduced many to the technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1042" data-file-width="899" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg/170px-Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg/255px-Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg/340px-Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Keith_Richards_Hannover_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Keith Richards, 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Rolling Stones ended the 1990s with the album <i><a href="/wiki/Bridges_to_Babylon" title="Bridges to Babylon">Bridges to Babylon</a></i> (UK 6; US 3), released in 1997 to mixed reviews. The video of the single "<a href="/wiki/Anybody_Seen_My_Baby%3F" title="Anybody Seen My Baby?">Anybody Seen My Baby?</a>" featured <a href="/wiki/Angelina_Jolie" title="Angelina Jolie">Angelina Jolie</a> as guest and met steady rotation on both MTV and VH1. Sales were reasonably equivalent to those of previous records (about 1.2 million copies sold in the US), and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Bridges_to_Babylon_Tour" title="Bridges to Babylon Tour">Bridges to Babylon Tour</a>, which crossed Europe, North America and other destinations, proved the band to be a strong live attraction. Once again, a live album was culled from the tour, <i><a href="/wiki/No_Security" title="No Security">No Security</a></i> (UK 67; US 34), only this time all but two songs ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_With_Me" title="Live With Me">Live With Me</a>" and "The Last Time") were previously unreleased on live albums. In 1999, the Rolling Stones staged the <a href="/wiki/No_Security_Tour" title="No Security Tour">No Security Tour</a> in the US and continued the Bridges to Babylon tour in Europe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.E2.80.9311:_A_Bigger_Bang_and_continued_success">2000–11: <i>A Bigger Bang</i> and continued success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2000–11: A Bigger Bang and continued success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In late 2001, Mick Jagger released his fourth solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Goddess_in_the_Doorway" title="Goddess in the Doorway">Goddess in the Doorway</a></i> (UK 44; US 39) which met with mixed reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> A month after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, Jagger and Richards took part in "<a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City" title="The Concert for New York City">The Concert for New York City</a>", performing "<a href="/wiki/Salt_of_the_Earth_(song)" title="Salt of the Earth (song)">Salt of the Earth</a>" and "Miss You" with a backing band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, the band released <i><a href="/wiki/Forty_Licks" title="Forty Licks">Forty Licks</a></i> (UK 2; US 2), a greatest hits double album, to mark their forty years as a band. The collection contained four new songs recorded with the latter-day core band of Jagger, Richards, Watts, Wood, Leavell and Jones. The album has sold more than 7 million copies worldwide. The same year, <a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)"><i>Q</i> magazine</a> named the Rolling Stones as one of the "50 Bands To See Before You Die",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> and the 2002–2003 <a href="/wiki/Licks_Tour" title="Licks Tour">Licks Tour</a> gave people that chance. The tour included shows in small theatres. The band headlined the <a href="/wiki/Molson_Canadian_Rocks_for_Toronto" title="Molson Canadian Rocks for Toronto">Molson Canadian Rocks for Toronto</a> concert in Toronto, Ontario, Canada, to help the city – which they have used for rehearsals since the Steel Wheels tour – recover from the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Severe_acute_respiratory_syndrome" title="Severe acute respiratory syndrome">SARS</a> epidemic. The concert was attended by an estimated 490,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 November 2003, the band played their first concert in Hong Kong as part of the <a href="/wiki/Harbour_Fest" title="Harbour Fest">Harbour Fest</a> celebration, also in support of the SARS-affected economy. In November 2003, the band exclusively licensed the right to sell their new four-DVD boxed set, <i><a href="/wiki/Four_Flicks" title="Four Flicks">Four Flicks</a></i>, recorded on the band's most recent world tour, to the US <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a> chain of stores. In response, some Canadian and US music retail chains (including <a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a> Canada and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circuit_City_(1949%E2%80%932009_company)" title="Circuit City (1949–2009 company)">Circuit City</a>) pulled Rolling Stones CDs and related merchandise from their shelves and replaced them with signs explaining the situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, a double live album of the Licks Tour, <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Licks" title="Live Licks">Live Licks</a></i> (UK 38; US 50), was released, going gold in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_144-2"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2004, the Rolling Stones were among the inaugural inductees into the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="683" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg/220px-Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg/330px-Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg/440px-Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_stones_-_11_luglio_2006_-_san_siro.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Rolling Stones, 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 26 July 2005, Jagger's birthday, the band announced the name of their new album, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bigger_Bang" title="A Bigger Bang">A Bigger Bang</a></i> (UK 2; US 3), their first album in almost eight years. <i>A Bigger Bang</i> was released on 6 September to strong reviews, including a glowing write-up in <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The single "<a href="/wiki/Streets_of_Love" title="Streets of Love">Streets of Love</a>" reached the top 15 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialcharts_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-officialcharts-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album included the political "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_Neo_Con" title="Sweet Neo Con">Sweet Neo Con</a>", a criticism of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoconservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Neoconservatism in the United States">American Neoconservatism</a> from Jagger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was reportedly almost dropped from the album because of objections from Richards. When asked if he was afraid of political backlash such as the <a href="/wiki/Dixie_Chicks" title="Dixie Chicks">Dixie Chicks</a> had endured, Richards responded that the album came first, and that, "I don't want to be sidetracked by some little political 'storm in a teacup'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The subsequent <a href="/wiki/A_Bigger_Bang_(concert_tour)" title="A Bigger Bang (concert tour)">A Bigger Bang Tour</a> began in August 2005, and visited North America, South America and East Asia. In February 2006, the group played the half-time show of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XL" title="Super Bowl XL">Super Bowl XL</a> in Detroit, Michigan. By the end of 2005, the Bigger Bang tour set a record of $162 million in gross receipts, breaking the North American mark also set by the Rolling Stones 1994. On 18 February 2006 the band played a free concert to over one million people at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copacabana_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" title="Copacabana (Rio de Janeiro)">Copacabana beach</a> in Rio de Janeiro; one of the biggest rock concerts of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG/220px-ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG/330px-ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG/440px-ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ABiggerBangTwickenham2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Rolling Stones at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a>, London during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Bigger_Bang_Tour" title="A Bigger Bang Tour">A Bigger Bang Tour</a> in August 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After performances in Japan, China, Australia and New Zealand in March/April 2006, the Rolling Stones tour took a scheduled break before proceeding to Europe; during this break Keith Richards was hospitalised in New Zealand for cranial surgery after a fall from a tree on <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, where he had been on holiday. The incident led to a six-week delay in launching the European leg of the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kiwi_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-kiwi-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2006 it was reported that Ronnie Wood was continuing his programme of rehabilitation for alcohol abuse,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> but this did not affect the rearranged European tour schedule. Two out of the 21 shows scheduled for July–September 2006 were later cancelled due to Mick Jagger's throat problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iorreuro2006_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-iorreuro2006-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Rolling Stones returned to North America for concerts in September 2006, and returned to Europe on 5 June 2007. By November 2006, the Bigger Bang tour had been declared the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_highest_grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest grossing concert tours">highest grossing tour</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Rolling Stones performances at New York City's <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Theatre_(New_York_City)" title="Beacon Theatre (New York City)">Beacon Theatre</a> on 29 October and 1 November 2006 were filmed by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> for a documentary film, <i><a href="/wiki/Shine_a_Light_(film)" title="Shine a Light (film)">Shine a Light</a></i>, which was released in 2008. The film also features guest appearances by <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jack_White_(musician)" title="Jack White (musician)">Jack White</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> An accompanying soundtrack, also titled <i><a href="/wiki/Shine_a_Light_(The_Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Shine a Light (The Rolling Stones album)">Shine a Light</a></i> (UK 2; US 11), was released in April 2008. The album's debut at number 2 in the UK charts was the highest position for a Rolling Stones concert album since <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Yer_Ya-Ya%27s_Out!_The_Rolling_Stones_in_Concert" title="Get Yer Ya-Ya's Out! The Rolling Stones in Concert">Get Yer Ya-Ya's Out! The Rolling Stones in Concert</a></i> in 1970. At the Beacon Theater show, Music Executive, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmet_Ertegun" title="Ahmet Ertegun">Ahmet Ertegun</a> fell and ultimately succumbed to his injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 March 2007, the band announced a tour of Europe called the "Bigger Bang 2007" tour. 12 June 2007 saw the release of the band's second four-disc DVD set: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Biggest_Bang" title="The Biggest Bang">The Biggest Bang</a></i>, a seven-hour document featuring their shows in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a>, Rio de Janeiro, <a href="/wiki/Saitama,_Saitama" title="Saitama, Saitama">Saitama</a>, Shanghai and <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, along with extras. On 10 June 2007, the band performed their first gig at a festival in 30 years, at the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_Festival" title="Isle of Wight Festival">Isle of Wight Festival</a>, to a crowd of 65,000, and were joined onstage by <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse" title="Amy Winehouse">Amy Winehouse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> On 26 August 2007, they played their last concert of the Bigger Bang tour at <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">The O2 Arena</a> in London. At the conclusion of the tour, the band had grossed a record setting $558 million and were listed in the latest edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Mick Jagger released a compilation of his solo work called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Very_Best_of_Mick_Jagger" title="The Very Best of Mick Jagger">The Very Best of Mick Jagger</a></i> (UK 57; US 77), including three unreleased songs, on 2 October 2007. On 12 November 2007, ABKCO released <i><a href="/wiki/Rolled_Gold:_The_Very_Best_of_the_Rolling_Stones" title="Rolled Gold: The Very Best of the Rolling Stones">Rolled Gold: The Very Best of the Rolling Stones</a></i>, a double-CD remake of the 1975 compilation <i>Rolled Gold</i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="632" data-file-width="901" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg/220px-Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg/330px-Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg/440px-Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_Berlinale_Filmfestspiele_2008_Berlin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Rolling Stones in 2008 (from left to right: Watts, Wood, Richards, Jagger) at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berlin_Film_Festival" title="Berlin Film Festival">Berlin Film Festival</a>'s world premiere of Martin Scorsese's documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Shine_a_Light_(film)" title="Shine a Light (film)">Shine a Light</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In a 2007 interview with Mick Jagger after nearly two years of touring, Jagger refused to say when the band is going to retire: "I'm sure the Rolling Stones will do more things, more records and more tours, we've got no plans to stop any of that, really. As far as I'm concerned, I'm sure we'll continue."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2008 Keith Richards sparked rumours that a new Rolling Stones studio album may be forthcoming, saying during an interview following the premiere of <i>Shine a Light</i>, "I think we might make another album. Once we get over doing promotion on this film". Drummer Charlie Watts remarked that he got ill whenever he stopped working.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2008 it was announced that the Rolling Stones were leaving EMI and signing with Vivendi's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Music" title="Universal Music">Universal Music</a>, taking with them their catalogue stretching back to <i>Sticky Fingers</i>. New music released by the band while under this contract will be issued through Universal's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polydor" title="Polydor">Polydor</a> label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Records" title="Mercury Records">Mercury Records</a> will hold the US rights to the pre-1994 material, while the post-1994 material will be handled by <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> (once a subsidiary of Atlantic).</p>
<p>During the autumn, Mick Jagger and Keith Richards worked with producer Don Was to add new vocals and guitar parts to ten unfinished songs from the <i><a href="/wiki/Exile_on_Main_St." title="Exile on Main St.">Exile on Main St.</a></i> sessions. Jagger and Mick Taylor also did a session together in London where Taylor added lead guitar to what would be the expanded album's single, "<a href="/wiki/Plundered_My_Soul" title="Plundered My Soul">Plundered My Soul</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> On 17 April 2010, the band released a limited edition 7-inch vinyl single of the previously unreleased track "Plundered My Soul" in honour of <a href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day" title="Record Store Day">Record Store Day</a>. The track, part of the group's 2010 re-issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Exile_on_Main_St." title="Exile on Main St.">Exile on Main St.</a></i>, was combined with "<a href="/wiki/All_Down_the_Line" title="All Down the Line">All Down the Line</a>" as its <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">B-side</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> The band appeared at Cannes Festival for the premiere of the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Stones_in_Exile" title="Stones in Exile">Stones in Exile</a></i> (directed by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Kijak" title="Stephen Kijak">Stephen Kijak</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cannes_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cannes-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup>) about the recording of the album <i>Exile on Main St.</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cannes_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cannes-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> On 23 May, the re-issue of <i>Exile on Main St.</i> reached No. 1 in the UK charts, almost 38 years to the week after it first occupied that position, with the band becoming the first act ever to see a classic work return to No. 1 decades after it was first released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> In the US, the album re-entered the charts at No. 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 October 2010, the Stones released <i><a href="/wiki/Ladies_and_Gentlemen:_The_Rolling_Stones" title="Ladies and Gentlemen: The Rolling Stones">Ladies and Gentlemen: The Rolling Stones</a></i> to the cinemas and later on to DVD. A digitally remastered version of the film was shown in select cinemas across the United States. This live performance was recorded during 4 shows in Ft. Worth and Houston, Texas in support of their <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones_American_Tour_1972" title="The Rolling Stones American Tour 1972">The Rolling Stones American Tour 1972</a> and their album <i>Exile on Main St.</i>. The film was released to cinemas in 1974 but until now it was never available for home release apart from the numerous bootleg copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 October 2011, the Stones released <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones:_Some_Girls_Live_In_Texas_%2778" title="The Rolling Stones: Some Girls Live In Texas '78">The Rolling Stones: Some Girls Live In Texas '78</a></i> to the cinemas and later on to DVD. A digitally remastered version of the film was shown in select cinemas across the US. This live performance was recorded during one show in Ft. Worth, Texas in support of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_US_Tour_1978" title="Rolling Stones US Tour 1978">US Tour 1978</a> and their album <i>Some Girls</i>. The film was released in (DVD/<a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a>) on 15 November 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> On 21 November, the Stones reissued their 1978 album <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Girls" title="Some Girls">Some Girls</a></i> as a 2 CD deluxe edition with a second CD of twelve previously unreleased tracks (except "So Young," which was a b-side to "<a href="/wiki/Out_of_Tears" title="Out of Tears">Out of Tears</a>") from the sessions for <i>Some Girls</i>, like the 2010 reissue of <i>Exile On Main St.</i>, with mostly newly recorded vocals from Jagger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.93present:_50th_anniversary">2012–present: 50th anniversary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2012–present: 50th anniversary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1925" data-file-width="1915" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg/220px-Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg/330px-Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg/440px-Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_Keith_Richards_Rolling_Stones_2012-12-13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger and Richards on stage in December 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Rolling Stones celebrated their 50th anniversary in the summer of 2012 by releasing a large hardback book titled <i>50</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> A new take on the band's lip-and-tongue logo, designed by Shepard Fairey, was also released and used during the celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The documentary titled <i>Crossfire Hurricane</i>, directed by Brett Morgen, was released in October 2012. Approximately fifty hours of interviews were conducted by Morgen for use for the documentary, including interviews with Bill Wyman and Mick Taylor, which Morgen says are "the most extensive group interviews they've ever done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> This would be the first official career-spanning documentary since 1989's <i><a href="/wiki/25x5:_The_Continuing_Adventures_of_the_Rolling_Stones" title="25x5: The Continuing Adventures of the Rolling Stones">25x5: The Continuing Adventures of the Rolling Stones</a></i>, which was filmed for their 25th anniversary in 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A new compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/GRRR!" title="GRRR!">GRRR!</a></i>, was released on 12 November, available in four different formats and including two new tracks, "<a href="/wiki/Doom_and_Gloom" title="Doom and Gloom">Doom and Gloom</a>" and "One More Shot", which were recorded at Studio Guillaume Tell in Paris, France, within the last few weeks of August 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted at No. 3 in the UK and No. 19 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialcharts_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-officialcharts-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video for "Doom and Gloom" featuring <a href="/wiki/Noomi_Rapace" title="Noomi Rapace">Noomi Rapace</a> was released on 20 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Rolling_Stones,_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Rolling_Stones%2C_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg/220px-The_Rolling_Stones%2C_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Rolling_Stones%2C_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg/330px-The_Rolling_Stones%2C_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Rolling_Stones%2C_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg/440px-The_Rolling_Stones%2C_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Rolling_Stones,_Prudential_Center_2012-12-13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stage set for the <a href="/wiki/50_%26_Counting" title="50 &amp; Counting">50 &amp; Counting</a> tour at the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Center" title="Prudential Center">Prudential Center</a>, New Jersey</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 25 November 2012, the Stones commenced their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50_%26_Counting..." title="50 &amp; Counting...">50 &amp; Counting...</a> tour at London's <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">O2 Arena</a>, where they were joined by <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> At their second show in London on 29 November the group were joined onstage by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florence_Welch" title="Florence Welch">Florence Welch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anniversayconcerts_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-anniversayconcerts-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> Their third anniversary concert took place on 8 December at the <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a>, Brooklyn, New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anniversayconcerts_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-anniversayconcerts-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> The last two dates were at the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Center" title="Prudential Center">Prudential Center</a> in Newark, New Jersey on 13 and 15 December, and the band were joined by <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> and blues rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Keys" title="The Black Keys">The Black Keys</a> on the final night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anniversayconcerts_194-2"><a href="#cite_note-anniversayconcerts-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> They also played two songs at <i><a href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief" title="12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief">12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Stones played nineteen shows in the US in spring 2013, before playing three shows in Europe, one at <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival_2013" title="Glastonbury Festival 2013">Glastonbury Festival 2013</a> and two in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a>, London. On <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bacon_(broadcaster)" title="Richard Bacon (broadcaster)">Richard Bacon</a>'s <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a> show on 3 April 2013 it was announced that the Stones would hold a concert in Hyde Park as part of their 50th anniversary celebrations, although unlike their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stones_in_the_Park" title="Stones in the Park">1969 performance</a> in the park it would not be free, tickets being £95 each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCr5_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCr5-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger quipped, "I'll try and keep the poetry to a minimum," and remarked, in respect of the white dress that he wore for the 1969 concert, "I can still just about get into the zippers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCr5_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCr5-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> Richards announced 9 April 2013 on <i>Late Night with Jimmy Fallon</i> that Mick Taylor would be performing with the band for shows on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50_%26_Counting..." title="50 &amp; Counting...">50 &amp; Counting...</a> tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> The Rolling Stones made their Glastonbury debut, headlining on Saturday 29 June 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park_Live" title="Hyde Park Live">Hyde Park Live</a></i>, a live album recorded at Hyde Park on 6 and 13 July 2013, was released exclusively as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Online_distribution" title="Online distribution">digital download</a> through <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> on 22 July 2013 and peaked at No. 16 in the UK and No. 19 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> A live DVD, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_Summer_Sun:_Live_in_Hyde_Park" title="Sweet Summer Sun: Live in Hyde Park">Sweet Summer Sun: Live in Hyde Park</a></i>, was released on 11 November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2014, the band embarked on the "14 On Fire" tour spanning Middle East, Asia, Australia and Europe due to last until Summer 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> On 17 March 2014, the sudden death in New York City of <a href="/wiki/L%27Wren_Scott" title="L'Wren Scott">L'Wren Scott</a>, the longtime girlfriend/partner of Jagger, was reported by various news sources as the Rolling Stones were in Australia preparing for their first show in Perth. It was announced on their website that those shows were cancelled for that reason, and would be rescheduled at a later date. On 15 April 2014, the band announced that they had rescheduled their Australian tour to start at the newly revamped <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Oval" title="Adelaide Oval">Adelaide Oval</a> on 25 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 June 2014, the Rolling Stones performed for the first time in Israel with the <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> newspaper going as far as describing the concert as being "Historic with a capital H".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> To an extent, The Stones' Israeli debut provided a means of closure vis-à-vis the early background of rock and roll in Israel; in 1965, Prime Minister David Ben Gurion and numerous politicians in the Knesset, Israel's parliament, had believed at the time that rock and roll performances might corrupt the minds of the Israeli youth. Accordingly, the State of Israel had cancelled scheduled performances of notable artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_development">Musical development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Musical development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Rolling Stones are notable in modern popular music for assimilating various musical genres into their own collective sound. Throughout the band's career, their musical contributions have been marked by a continual reference and reliance on musical styles including blues, rhythm and blues, country, folk, reggae, dance, and <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>, exemplified by Jones' collaboration with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_Musicians_of_Jajouka" title="Master Musicians of Jajouka">Master Musicians of Jajouka</a>, as well as traditional English styles that use stringed instrumentation like harps. Brian Jones experimented with the use of non-traditional instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Sitar" title="Sitar">sitar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slide_guitar" title="Slide guitar">slide guitar</a> in their early days. The group started out covering early rock 'n' roll and blues songs, and have never stopped playing live or recording <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cover_song" title="Cover song">cover songs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LARS_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-LARS-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LARS_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-LARS-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infusion_of_American_blues">Infusion of American blues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Infusion of American blues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jagger and Richards shared an admiration of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Reed" title="Jimmy Reed">Jimmy Reed</a>, Muddy Waters, and <a href="/wiki/Little_Walter" title="Little Walter">Little Walter</a>, and their interest influenced Brian Jones, of whom Richards says, "He was more into <a href="/wiki/T-Bone_Walker" title="T-Bone Walker">T-Bone Walker</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jazz_blues" title="Jazz blues">jazz blues</a> stuff. We'd turn him onto Chuck Berry and say, 'Look, it's all the same shit, man, and you can do it.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenfield1981_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreenfield1981-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Charlie Watts, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_jazz" title="Traditional jazz">traditional jazz</a> drummer, was also introduced to the blues through his association with the pair. "Keith and Brian turned me on to Jimmy Reed and people like that. I learned that Earl Phillips was playing on those records like a jazz drummer, playing swing, with a straight four."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200341_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200341-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger, recalling when he first heard the likes of Chuck Berry, Bo Diddley, Muddy Waters, <a href="/wiki/Fats_Domino" title="Fats Domino">Fats Domino</a>, and other major American R&amp;B artists, said it "seemed the most real thing"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> he had heard up to that point. Similarly, Keith Richards, describing the first time he listened to Muddy Waters, said it was the "most powerful music [he had] ever heard ... the most expressive."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> He also stated, "when you think of some dopey, spotty seventeen year old from Dartford, who wants to be Muddy Waters-- and there were a lot of us-- in a way, very pathetic, but in another way, very ... heartwarming".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richardsblues_1963_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Richardsblues_1963-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_songwriting">Early songwriting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Early songwriting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite the Rolling Stones' predilection for blues and R&amp;B numbers on their early live setlists, the first original compositions by the band reflected a more wide-ranging interest. The first Jagger/Richards single, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tell_Me_(You%27re_Coming_Back)" title="Tell Me (You're Coming Back)">Tell Me (You're Coming Back)</a>", has been described by critic <a href="/wiki/Richie_Unterberger" title="Richie Unterberger">Richie Unterberger</a> as a "<a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a> ballad ... When [Jagger and Richards] began to write songs, they were usually not derived from the blues, but were often surprisingly fey, slow, <a href="/wiki/Beat_music" title="Beat music">Mersey</a>-type pop numbers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/As_Tears_Go_By_(song)" title="As Tears Go By (song)">As Tears Go By</a>", the ballad originally written for Marianne Faithfull, was one of the first songs written by Jagger and Richards and also one of many written by the duo for other artists. Jagger said of the song, "It's a relatively mature song considering the rest of the output at the time. And we didn't think of [recording] it, because The Rolling Stones were a butch blues group."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> The Rolling Stones did later record a version which became a top five hit in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On the early experience, Richards said, "The amazing thing is that although Mick and I thought these songs were really puerile and kindergarten-time, every one that got put out made a decent showing in the charts. That gave us extraordinary confidence to carry on, because at the beginning songwriting was something we were going to do in order to say to Andrew [Loog Oldham], 'Well, at least we gave it a try ...'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200385_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200385-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger said, "We were very pop-orientated. We didn't sit around listening to Muddy Waters; we listened to everything. In some ways it's easy to write to order ... Keith and I got into the groove of writing those kind of tunes; they were done in ten minutes. I think we thought it was a bit of a laugh, and it turned out to be something of an apprenticeship for us."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200385_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200385-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The writing of "The Last Time", the Rolling Stones' first major single, proved a turning point. Richards called it "a bridge into thinking about writing for the Stones. It gave us a level of confidence; a pathway of how to do it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200395_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaggerRichardsWattsWood200395-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was based on a traditional gospel song popularised by <a href="/wiki/The_Staple_Singers" title="The Staple Singers">the Staple Singers</a>, but the Rolling Stones' number features a distinctive guitar riff, played by Brian Jones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to the emergence of Jagger/Richards as the Stones' songwriters, the band members occasionally were given collective credit under the pseudonym <a href="/wiki/Nanker_Phelge" title="Nanker Phelge">Nanker Phelge</a>. Some songs attributed to Nanker Phelge have been re-attributed to Jagger/Richards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Band_members">Band members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Band members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tours">Tours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones_concerts" title="The Rolling Stones concerts">The Rolling Stones concerts</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="noprint portal tright" style="border:solid #aaa 1px;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em">
